  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_227595df-988d-4070-b0ec-dab75e5e2cb2'

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1146822736879470808">Over ten years ago, Air Force major Nick Baron was part of a failed special ops mission that left a B-2 stealth bomber at the bottom of the Persian Gulf. Now, leading his men—the Triple Seven Chase team—Baron must find the bomber and dispose of it for good before any unfriendly nation can steal the onboard technology for its own purposes. But as the team embarks on its mis</span>
  <span id="freeText1146822736879470808" style="display:none">Over ten years ago, Air Force major Nick Baron was part of a failed special ops mission that left a B-2 stealth bomber at the bottom of the Persian Gulf. Now, leading his men—the Triple Seven Chase team—Baron must find the bomber and dispose of it for good before any unfriendly nation can steal the onboard technology for its own purposes. But as the team embarks on its mission, there are greater dangers waiting.<p>When the CIA intercepts a call signal from an operative in China long thought dead, the Triple Seven Chase team is given the perilous task of retrieving the lone soldier from deep within the Chinese wilderness. There is only one plane for such a dangerous mission: the Shadow Catcher, a plane with capabilities beyond anything that has ever flown.</p><p>What Baron and his men don’t know is that the enemy is already among them—and that the Shadow Catcher itself may be the ultimate prize.</p></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer934945023838689342">"This is our foxhole, and in foxholes, sometimes faith is all you've got."<br/><br/>"Shadow Catcher" is an exciting military techno thriller. It was plot-driven rather than character-based but aren't most military thrillers?<br/><br/>Some military thrillers I just can't get into because of an overabundance of military jargon and acronyms but this one had a nice balance of military and personal drama and author Hannibal explained the military subject matter in a way that was easy to understand. He was also able to d</span>
  <span id="freeText934945023838689342" style="display:none">"This is our foxhole, and in foxholes, sometimes faith is all you've got."<br /><br />"Shadow Catcher" is an exciting military techno thriller. It was plot-driven rather than character-based but aren't most military thrillers?<br /><br />Some military thrillers I just can't get into because of an overabundance of military jargon and acronyms but this one had a nice balance of military and personal drama and author Hannibal explained the military subject matter in a way that was easy to understand. He was also able to do this without foul language and extraneous sex scenes.<br /><br />A B-2 stealth bomber sitting on the bottom of the Persian Gulf, the Triple Seven Case team, a POW missing since 1988, the Shadow Catcher, Nick Baron and all his team including a frustrating newbie, espionage, a deadly mole burrowed in, plus much more are tied together in this rollicking but dangerous tale of rescue and intrigue.<br /><br />I will definitely be keeping my eyes open for more tales by author Hannibal.<br /><br />NOTE: I received a copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.</span>

<div id="review_750147920" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/750147920" />
    <a title="Ryan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25083629-ryan"><img alt="Ryan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416502587p2/25083629.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/750147920?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan" href="/user/show/25083629-ryan">Ryan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer750147920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8347149158528292522">Exciting and thought-provoking! This is not your run-of-the-mill techno-thriller. Hannibal knows his topic from real-world experience as a stealth pilot, and he definitely makes the tech a character in the story. But there is much more to be found here than gee-whiz gadgets. Shadow Catcher is a mystery, a spy-vs-spy hunt for a mole that we can't be sure even exists. It is also psychological, following Nick Baron's struggle to come to grips with the PTSD that is fueling is self-doubt and paranoia</span>
  <span id="freeText8347149158528292522" style="display:none">Exciting and thought-provoking! This is not your run-of-the-mill techno-thriller. Hannibal knows his topic from real-world experience as a stealth pilot, and he definitely makes the tech a character in the story. But there is much more to be found here than gee-whiz gadgets. Shadow Catcher is a mystery, a spy-vs-spy hunt for a mole that we can't be sure even exists. It is also psychological, following Nick Baron's struggle to come to grips with the PTSD that is fueling is self-doubt and paranoia and driving a wedge between him and his wife. Fun and literary at the same time - this book is the whole package.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8347149158528292522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_774607961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/774607961" />
    <a title="Keith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12854895-keith"><img alt="Keith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470249157p2/12854895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/774607961?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keith" href="/user/show/12854895-keith">Keith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer774607961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6043443849540592898">A surprisingly good read. I really enjoyed Shadow Catcher. The characters are more interesting than what you usually find in military fiction, and their relationships, or lack thereof, work well. Mr. Hannibal does a nice job with each character's backstory, so when the payoffs come, they are believable. Shadow Catcher is no The Hunt for Red October, but then again what is? Honestly, this book reminds me more of a vintage Clive Cussler story than the grittier thrillers we see today. It rolls at a</span>
  <span id="freeText6043443849540592898" style="display:none">A surprisingly good read. I really enjoyed Shadow Catcher. The characters are more interesting than what you usually find in military fiction, and their relationships, or lack thereof, work well. Mr. Hannibal does a nice job with each character's backstory, so when the payoffs come, they are believable. Shadow Catcher is no The Hunt for Red October, but then again what is? Honestly, this book reminds me more of a vintage Clive Cussler story than the grittier thrillers we see today. It rolls at a break-neck pace, and while predictable, give the reader more than his money's worth. Once it started rolling toward its conclusion, I found it VERY hard to put down. Four stars. Recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6043443849540592898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1258169438" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1258169438" />
    <a title="Shaun" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25572202-shaun"><img alt="Shaun" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442962175p2/25572202.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1258169438?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaun" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaun" href="/user/show/25572202-shaun">Shaun</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1258169438" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9577540681462902869">Shadow Catcher… I think from reading the back of the book, I was expecting a more techno-military thriller along the lines of Clancy, but actually I think this book reads a tad more like Cussler. The two seemingly main characters in the series, Drake and Nick, seemed to have an Al Giordino and Dirk Pitt vibe. Although I think this is the second book in the series (never read anything else by the author), it was a bit unique in that it felt more like this was the tenth book in the series, like th</span>
  <span id="freeText9577540681462902869" style="display:none">Shadow Catcher… I think from reading the back of the book, I was expecting a more techno-military thriller along the lines of Clancy, but actually I think this book reads a tad more like Cussler. The two seemingly main characters in the series, Drake and Nick, seemed to have an Al Giordino and Dirk Pitt vibe. Although I think this is the second book in the series (never read anything else by the author), it was a bit unique in that it felt more like this was the tenth book in the series, like the characters already had a ton of history, and had been through the fire a few times.<br /><br />There are a few problems I had with this book, beginning with… empathy. Although the writing and story was okay, none of the characters really seemed to grab me. The only one I had a shred of empathy for really was Quinn. In many ways, I think the book sort of has three parts, which I’ll try to disclose without spoilers – bomber retrieval, team building, and mission. The first ‘act’, if you will, just didn’t seem to mean much for me when the story was said and done. While I suppose it functions as getting across some backstory and beginning with some action, I just don’t feel like it was necessary for the plot. Again, it was fine, but when I finished the book, I just sort of thought back and wondered what that first third of the book had to do with the rest of the story. <br /><br />In a large way, this book just lacks…. oomph, to me. The lack of interest I had in the characters probably had something to do with that, and then just the time it took to get to the main story. It just felt like something was missing, or was there but wasn’t supposed to be there. Either way, something was off. <br /><br />But I liked it well enough. It feels very much like a second or third novel, with room for improvement, but beginning to get its foothold. Almost there, but not quite. So I’ll rate it three stairs. Liked it. Didn’t love it. Would be open to reading another book from the author, particularly a book after this one, whether in the same series or a different series doesn’t matter so much. I’d just be curious to see if he improves on this novel or not in the next one, if there is a next one. So! Three stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9577540681462902869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_834591350" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/834591350" />
    <a title="Alan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4131838-alan"><img alt="Alan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414009631p2/4131838.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/834591350?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alan" href="/user/show/4131838-alan">Alan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer834591350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7041991244258855491">I have been a fan of the military techno thriller since Tom Clancy made that genre popular in mid-1980s. I am therefore often on the lookout for authors who craft engaging stories in that genre. James Hannibal was my most recent hope.<br/><br/>I dove into "Shadow Catcher" with high hopes. Hannibal did his best to employ a layered story telling approach as he unfolded his story, but I have to admit that after about the first 1/4 of the book I was experiencing something akin to mental whiplash as the book j</span>
  <span id="freeText7041991244258855491" style="display:none">I have been a fan of the military techno thriller since Tom Clancy made that genre popular in mid-1980s. I am therefore often on the lookout for authors who craft engaging stories in that genre. James Hannibal was my most recent hope.<br /><br />I dove into "Shadow Catcher" with high hopes. Hannibal did his best to employ a layered story telling approach as he unfolded his story, but I have to admit that after about the first 1/4 of the book I was experiencing something akin to mental whiplash as the book jumped from one time period to another, including flashbacks and dreams, and I had a hard time figuring out where the author was going. At times it didn't feel like he knew. The book's storyline started to settle into a more settled rhythm about halfway through. The end, though, was completely melodramatic. It felt like one of those 1950s cowboy movies...you know, when the narrator ties everything up in a nice tight little bundle, there is cheering, and adoration from the saved town folk.<br /><br />Unsurprisingly, this book is entirely plot-driven. There is precious little character development, only enough to keep the plot rolling. The plot did not drag, and for that I am grateful.<br /><br />So, what's in the book? Oh, a high-tech black ops team that seems able to do everything from marine salvage to ground ops to piloting ultra-secret aircraft, etc. There are also assassins, a kidnapper, at least one sociopath, and a plan that could bring the world to the brink of a world war. Did I leave anything out?<br /><br />This was a fun read once I finally managed to clear the first 1/4 of the book, but in the end was only OK.<br /><br />As Amazon's rating system indicates, 3 stars means that "It's okay". That's what it was to me...okay.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7041991244258855491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37060155-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1837351816?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/37060155-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37060155-mike?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1837351816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3611468158325607339">The author was new to me when I found _Shadow Catcher_ sitting on the shelf in the thrillers section of the bookstore. It has a B-2 on the cover, the author flew B-2's & A-10's (my favorite plane), so I thought this would be something along the lines of a Dale Brown type of book. Oh, so wrong. <br/><br/>The primary good guy characters are B-2 pilots who act like SEALs. Most of the book centers around them on the ground. Any flying is mundane, even when they have to enter super contested airspace of China </span>
  <span id="freeText3611468158325607339" style="display:none">The author was new to me when I found _Shadow Catcher_ sitting on the shelf in the thrillers section of the bookstore. It has a B-2 on the cover, the author flew B-2's &amp; A-10's (my favorite plane), so I thought this would be something along the lines of a Dale Brown type of book. Oh, so wrong. <br /><br />The primary good guy characters are B-2 pilots who act like SEALs. Most of the book centers around them on the ground. Any flying is mundane, even when they have to enter super contested airspace of China to land a super secret STOL plane. Nope, just fly in, land and then talk about the weather. <br /><br />All of the characters exhibit one trait. The author attempts to lead the reader with red herrings, but isn't smooth. The dialogue either was wrong or playing to cliche. I almost stopped reading when one of the characters praises the Second Amendment for allowing him/her to have a gun in their house to defend themselves. Really.<br /><br />I always cringe when non-computer types attempt to use technical language to impress. It usually ends in groans. No programmer would be showing the images being scanned through, as that would eat cycles. It is what I'd expect to see on TV. Also clip != mag. <br /><br />In the end, it wasn't very good. Early Dale Brown or Larry Bond knew how to tell stories, have solid characters and also get the technical jargon correct (all things I look for). This book just came off as pilots wanting to be special operators.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3611468158325607339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_965441472" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/965441472" />
    <a title="LORI (Dollycas) CASWELL" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4770012-lori-dollycas-caswell"><img alt="LORI (Dollycas) CASWELL" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490370947p2/4770012.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/965441472?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LORI (Dollycas) CASWELL" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LORI (Dollycas) CASWELL" href="/user/show/4770012-lori-dollycas-caswell">LORI (Dollycas) CASWELL</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4770012-lori-dollycas-caswell?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer965441472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13373100791014160203"><br/><br/>Dollycas’s Thoughts<br/><br/>I have Mr. James R. Hannibal to thank for a heck of a book hangover. I started reading this book and couldn’t put it down.<br/><br/>James R. Hannibal is a veteran combat pilot with Top Secret clearance from the U.S. government and he writes what he knows and he does it really well. The thing I really appreciated was this story is written for people like me and the military jargon was kept to a minimum. My husband enjoys Tom Clancy but his stories sometimes read like a military handbook </span>
  <span id="freeText13373100791014160203" style="display:none"><br /><br />Dollycas’s Thoughts<br /><br />I have Mr. James R. Hannibal to thank for a heck of a book hangover. I started reading this book and couldn’t put it down.<br /><br />James R. Hannibal is a veteran combat pilot with Top Secret clearance from the U.S. government and he writes what he knows and he does it really well. The thing I really appreciated was this story is written for people like me and the military jargon was kept to a minimum. My husband enjoys Tom Clancy but his stories sometimes read like a military handbook and fail to keep my interest. That is not the case at all with Shadow Catcher. The author had me from page one and held on tight to the very last word.<br /><br />The book starts out with a prologue from 1988 and then goes into the story in 2013 so you know these things are going to connect and with some very clever twists that is exactly what happens.<br /><br />Hannibal has created some very engaging characters. Their back stories are meshed into the plot effortlessly. This reader came to care about them very quickly.<br /><br />The story moves at a breakneck speed so don’t pick it up thinking you are going to read just a chapter or two at a time. It just won’t happen.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13373100791014160203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9171566140172262223">Nick Baron is fighting an emotional and mental demon of which he isn't completely aware. Married with a newborn son, Baron travels around the world on missions he can't talk about.<br/><br/>On the other side of the world, Chinese General Zheng schemes to become the next minister and apprehend the latest and greatest war time technology.<br/><br/>Airforce pilot David Novak went down and was captured by the Chinese over ten years ago. When he finally escapes, he finds a forgotten refuge and contacts a world that has </span>
  <span id="freeText9171566140172262223" style="display:none">Nick Baron is fighting an emotional and mental demon of which he isn't completely aware. Married with a newborn son, Baron travels around the world on missions he can't talk about.<br /><br />On the other side of the world, Chinese General Zheng schemes to become the next minister and apprehend the latest and greatest war time technology.<br /><br />Airforce pilot David Novak went down and was captured by the Chinese over ten years ago. When he finally escapes, he finds a forgotten refuge and contacts a world that has forgotten him. Some even believe him dead.<br /><br />Baron thinks Novak really does exist and is still alive. As he races to rescue the forgotten pilot, Baron finds himself up against General Zheng in an effort to get both Novak and his stealth plane off enemy soil and safely back to America.<br /><br />Time and again Hannibal proves you don't need copious bloody and gory scenes to write an edge of your seat thrill ride. The blood is minimal but the excitement is not. I always have a hard time putting his books and, and this one is no exception.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer976009457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9915661104848402174">Wow, I never expected anything half this good. I had picked it based on it's title and didn't expect much, in fact I almost had dropped it after the first few chapters. I'm glad I didn't.<br/>The characters felt genuine, their baggage was reasonable, and their interactions with each other felt real. Nick was a great hero, he was neither perfect or crass like other characters in thrillers.<br/>This is the first book in a while (especially from a thriller) where I couldn't put it down, I was sympathetic and</span>
  <span id="freeText9915661104848402174" style="display:none">Wow, I never expected anything half this good. I had picked it based on it's title and didn't expect much, in fact I almost had dropped it after the first few chapters. I'm glad I didn't.<br />The characters felt genuine, their baggage was reasonable, and their interactions with each other felt real. Nick was a great hero, he was neither perfect or crass like other characters in thrillers.<br />This is the first book in a while (especially from a thriller) where I couldn't put it down, I was sympathetic and even sad towards some of the characters, and where my heart was literally beating out of my chest and I couldn't read the words fast enough.<br />Overall I'm very impressed by the author. I'll admit the ending was pretty cheesy, but I'll let it slide. I'm defiitely going to read more books by him.</span>

A "Must read!"</span>

<div id="review_733579912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/733579912" />
    <a title="Valerie Strand" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22585406-valerie-strand"><img alt="Valerie Strand" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374973444p2/22585406.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_2830324423" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2830324423" />
    <a title="Paul Weiss" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51664350-paul-weiss"><img alt="Paul Weiss" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453113069p2/51664350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2830324423?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Weiss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Weiss" href="/user/show/51664350-paul-weiss">Paul Weiss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51664350-paul-weiss?shelf=techno-thriller">techno-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2830324423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2711326003262412290"><i><b>“They were not supposed to be there.”</b><br/><br/>“Nick and Quinn were about to take an untested aircraft into the heavily defended airspace of a sovereign country, a country that the United States at least pretended to be friends with.” “There would be no rescue if the mission suddenly went pear-shaped.”</i> Well, no reader fond of techno-thrillers and geo-political potboilers could deny that Hannibal conceived of a plot scenario that contained a world of possibilities. A compromised stealth jet mission into Ch</span>
  <span id="freeText2711326003262412290" style="display:none"><i><b>“They were not supposed to be there.”</b><br /><br />“Nick and Quinn were about to take an untested aircraft into the heavily defended airspace of a sovereign country, a country that the United States at least pretended to be friends with.” “There would be no rescue if the mission suddenly went pear-shaped.”</i> Well, no reader fond of techno-thrillers and geo-political potboilers could deny that Hannibal conceived of a plot scenario that contained a world of possibilities. A compromised stealth jet mission into Chinese territory to rescue an American prisoner captured during a previously failed espionage mission falls afoul of a megalomaniacal rogue Chinese general with world dominance in mind starting with a unilateral re-establishment of Chinese dominance over Taiwan! Intriguing, don’t you think?<br /><br />That’s where the quality of <b>Shadow Catcher</b> started and, sadly, that’s also where it ended.<br /><br />The dialogue is stilted, the characters are cartoonish and stereotypical in the extreme, and the action sequences are so beyond realistic that they would undoubtedly embarrass Rambo screenplay writers whose segments got rejected because they were too absurd. Hannibal even shoehorned in an opportunity to give the American gods praise for the existence of the 2nd Amendment. Puhleez! Did you really have to do that?<br /><br />When I first found <b>Shadow Catchers</b> and read that plot outline, I had high hopes that I had found a sequence of novels I could add to my groaning TBR shelves. But, that isn’t going to happen and my copy of <b>Shadow Catchers</b> is on its way to the nearest Little Free Library box to find the next unsuspecting victim. Larry Bond and Dale Brown still rule.<br /><br />Not recommended.<br /><br />Paul Weiss</span>
  <a data-text-id="2711326003262412290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1786012242" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16176379-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357613630p2/16176379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1786012242?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/16176379-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1786012242&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1786012242" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1192430107324302399">OK, but not great. It took a while to get going. I didn't care a lot about the characters, they didn't seem fully three dimensional. The character development comes in one paragraph: Nick B has an epiphany. Lots of action, and it's all about the plot. At the end it felt like "3 guys defeat Chinese military" in an action scene that might have taken 15 minutes. Very clear lines of good vs. evil, therefore it's hard not to cheer for the good guys. I did finish the book, but I will think long and ha</span>
  <span id="freeText1192430107324302399" style="display:none">OK, but not great. It took a while to get going. I didn't care a lot about the characters, they didn't seem fully three dimensional. The character development comes in one paragraph: Nick B has an epiphany. Lots of action, and it's all about the plot. At the end it felt like "3 guys defeat Chinese military" in an action scene that might have taken 15 minutes. Very clear lines of good vs. evil, therefore it's hard not to cheer for the good guys. I did finish the book, but I will think long and hard before reading another by this author. Sorry, but it wasn't my "cup of tea."</span>

<div id="review_1132216544" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1132216544" />
    <a title="Luke Taylor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30710594-luke-taylor"><img alt="Luke Taylor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522269800p2/30710594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1132216544?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luke Taylor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luke Taylor" href="/user/show/30710594-luke-taylor">Luke Taylor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1132216544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10852880117299908781">Based on the tangibly militaristic yet visually arresting cover art, featuring a lone stealth bomber slicing through dusky skies, boxed in by rippling American and Chinese national flags, I immediately snatched up a copy of Shadow Catcher and headed for the checkout lanes as memories of air combat simulator games jolted through my mind. I assumed the technothriller would blend the unrealistically advanced warfare of the film Stealth with the politically illegal combat caper of the film Flight of</span>
  <span id="freeText10852880117299908781" style="display:none">Based on the tangibly militaristic yet visually arresting cover art, featuring a lone stealth bomber slicing through dusky skies, boxed in by rippling American and Chinese national flags, I immediately snatched up a copy of Shadow Catcher and headed for the checkout lanes as memories of air combat simulator games jolted through my mind. I assumed the technothriller would blend the unrealistically advanced warfare of the film Stealth with the politically illegal combat caper of the film Flight of the Intruder with maybe some of the cold war spy-heist of Firefox thrown in and was not surprised to get a chewy bite of air combat right out of the gate. I was, however, pleasantly strung along into the plot-driven tale with the treasure hunt-like recovery of a downed stealth bomber and the underwater action sequences surrounding this first act arc were every bit as muscular as I wanted them to be, but beautifully descriptive as well. James R. Hannibal’s excellence is best exemplified in his action set-pieces and physical confrontations and throughout the story, these scenes are authentically technical and cinematic. Shadow Catcher is a simple and tasty read, unintimidating and satisfying, swiftly-paced and heavy-laden with third act twists and humorous one-liners. Hannibal’s lightness in humorous passages shows range, and, whilst the humour wasn’t my favorite element of the story, it pleasantly contrasted with a technothriller’s naturally humorless tropes, rolling a crackling strike down the middle of entertainment’s broad-guttered bowling alley with originality and a sense of cleanliness completely bereft in today’s thriller market. Removing any and all traces of profanity from such a tale, Hannibal widened his demographics and I wish I had this book when I was much younger, and will quickly be loaning it to friends of mine in high school and junior high who loathe the idea of more wizards, vampires, and first kiss romances. Combat vet James R. Hannibal deserves a promotion for a skilled and saavy mission accomplished.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10852880117299908781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jayden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37297123-jayden"><img alt="Jayden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453485564p2/37297123.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer18227690169744257188">One final mission for the retired operative and one plane, "the shadow catcher" by James R. Hannibal. <br/>One retired operative, leading a 10 man team into a impossible mission. One plane sitting at the bottom of the Persian gulf and one man sitting in a POW camp in the middle of a Chinese forest. With the impossible mission on nicks shoulders and ten men's life's as well. It's up to him not to mess up.<br/>The author uses three main elements in this story to pull the reader in with the characters of the</span>
  <span id="freeText18227690169744257188" style="display:none">One final mission for the retired operative and one plane, "the shadow catcher" by James R. Hannibal. <br />One retired operative, leading a 10 man team into a impossible mission. One plane sitting at the bottom of the Persian gulf and one man sitting in a POW camp in the middle of a Chinese forest. With the impossible mission on nicks shoulders and ten men's life's as well. It's up to him not to mess up.<br />The author uses three main elements in this story to pull the reader in with the characters of the story. He first uses suspense, when nick baron gets the offer to do one final job, he picks out his perfect team. Once they leave who knew who was gonna come back. Next uses POV of all the characters. He shows everyone's point of view on the story and their story and their goodbyes to their family.<br />He lastly uses vivid description, Making it seem like you are there with the team in combat, on the greatest rescue mission ever. </span>

<div id="review_1731503771" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer11249163183282532094">In the grand tradition of Clancy, this is a new author I will follow! Excellent, classic thriller style read- engaging characters with issues- high-tech gadgetry and ripping action- this was a terrific read. If you like Dale Brown, Clancy, Cussler, etc...you have to check out James Hannibal's novels- I just ordered the next one in this series!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4l8tEgU7i/2GsiHPe2SpiEEOPZRgSZuhbDw9yLJa0bV+Oi9XG8F8EFmNA344hjnUUEjD7aWsrcl23P4sv2w+uQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wQiDPcrqp3v1COEzB+rXGz4cY2K1OmT/KXQJEJwODmtdbYF41BBQlio3w4JECEdHL1qdG3DfUpczlMr0kTjhZw==')})
  }

We will advance to recent centuries to see how the prayers, teaching, and examples of godly mothers have shaped evangelists, preachers, and stalwart defenders of the faith.
